<h4><span id="Ibn_Battuta.27s_description_of_Mecca"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ibn_Battuta's_description_of_Mecca">Ibn Battuta's description of Mecca</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ibn Battuta's description of Mecca">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>One of the most famous travelers to Mecca in the 14th century was a Moroccan scholar and traveler, <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battuta" title="Ibn Battuta">Ibn Battuta</a>. In his <i>rihla</i> (account), he provides a vast description of the city. Around the year 1327 CE or 729 AH, Ibn Battuta arrived at the holy city. Immediately, he says, it felt like a holy sanctuary, and thus. he started the rites of the pilgrimage. He remained in Mecca for three years and left in 1330 CE. During his second year in the holy city, he says his caravan arrived "with a great quantity of alms for the support of those who were staying in Mecca and Medina". While in Mecca, prayers were made for (not to) the King of Iraq and also for <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Salaheddin al-Ayyubi</a>, Sultan of Egypt and Syria at the Ka'bah. Battuta says the Ka'bah was large, but was destroyed and rebuilt smaller than the original and that it contained images of angels and prophets including Jesus, his mother Mary, and many others. Battuta describes the Ka'bah as an important part of Mecca due to the fact that many people make the pilgrimage to it. Battuta describes the people of the city as being humble and kind, and also willing to give a part of everything they had to someone who had nothing. The inhabitants of Mecca and the village itself, he says, were very clean. There was also a sense of elegance to the village.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Under the Ottomans</b>
</p><p>In 1517, the then Sharif of Mecca, Barakat bin Muhammad, acknowledged the supremacy of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate" title="Ottoman Caliphate">Ottoman Caliph</a> but retained a great degree of local autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> In 1803 the city was captured by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Saudi_State" title="First Saudi State">First Saudi State</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> which held Mecca until 1813, destroying some of the historic tombs and domes in and around the city. The Ottomans assigned the task of bringing Mecca back under Ottoman control to their powerful <i><a href="/wiki/Khedive" title="Khedive">Khedive</a></i> (viceroy) and <i><a href="/wiki/Wali_(administrative_title)" title="Wali (administrative title)">Wali</a></i> of Egypt, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">Muhammad Ali Pasha</a>. Muhammad Ali Pasha successfully returned Mecca to Ottoman control <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_return_of_Mecca_1813" title="Ottoman return of Mecca 1813">in 1813</a>. In 1818, the Saud were defeated again but survived and founded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Saudi_State" title="Second Saudi State">Second Saudi State</a> that lasted until 1891 and led on to the present country of Saudi Arabia. In 1853, Sir <a href="/wiki/Richard_Francis_Burton" title="Richard Francis Burton">Richard Francis Burton</a> undertook the Muslim pilgrimage to Mecca and Medina disguised as a Muslim. Although Burton was certainly not the first non-Muslim European to make the <i>Hajj</i> (<a href="/wiki/Ludovico_di_Varthema" title="Ludovico di Varthema">Ludovico di Varthema</a> did this in 1503),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> his pilgrimage remains one of the most famous and documented of modern times. Mecca was regularly hit by <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cholera_outbreaks_and_pandemics" title="Cholera outbreaks and pandemics">outbreaks</a>. Between 1830 and 1930, cholera broke out among pilgrims at Mecca 27 times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef,_Makkah,_Saudi_Arabia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2988" data-file-width="5312" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef%2C_Makkah%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/300px-Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef%2C_Makkah%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef%2C_Makkah%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/450px-Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef%2C_Makkah%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef%2C_Makkah%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/600px-Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef%2C_Makkah%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Surrounding_area_of_Haram_Shareef,_Makkah,_Saudi_Arabia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The area surrounding the Haram Shareef.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Hashemite Revolt and subsequent control by the Sharifate of Mecca</b>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the Ottoman Empire was at war with the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a>. It had successfully repulsed an attack on <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gallipoli_campaign" title="Gallipoli campaign">Gallipoli campaign</a> and on Baghdad in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kut" title="Siege of Kut">Siege of Kut</a>. The British intelligence agent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T.E._Lawrence" title="T.E. Lawrence">T.E. Lawrence</a> conspired with the Ottoman governor, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca" title="Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca">Hussain bin Ali</a>, the Sharif of Mecca to revolt against the Ottoman Empire and it was the first city captured by his forces in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mecca_(1916)" title="Battle of Mecca (1916)">1916 Battle of Mecca</a>. Sharif's revolt proved a turning point of the war on the eastern front. Hussein declared a new state, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hejaz" title="Kingdom of Hejaz">Kingdom of Hejaz</a>, declaring himself the Sharif of the state and Mecca his capital. News reports in November 1916 via contact in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> with returning <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> pilgrims, stated that with the Ottoman Turkish authorities gone, the Hajj of 1916 was free of the previous massive extortion and monetary demands made by the Turks who were agents of the Ottoman government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Saudi Arabian conquest and modern history</b>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mecca_(1924)" title="Battle of Mecca (1924)">1924 Battle of Mecca</a>, the Sharif of Mecca was overthrown by the Saud family, and Mecca was incorporated into Saudi Arabia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-87">[86]</a></sup> Under Saudi rule, much of the historic city has been demolished as a result of the Saudi government fearing these sites might become sites of association in worship besides Allah (<i><a href="/wiki/Shirk_(Islam)" title="Shirk (Islam)">shirk</a></i>). The city has been expanded to include several towns previously considered to be separate from the holy city and now is just a few kilometers outside the main sites of the Hajj, Mina, Muzdalifah and Arafat. Mecca is not served by any airport, due to concerns about the city's safety. It is instead served by the <a href="/wiki/King_Abdulaziz_International_Airport" title="King Abdulaziz International Airport">King Abdulaziz International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a> (approx. 70 km away) internationally and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%27if_Regional_Airport" title="Ta'if Regional Airport">Ta'if Regional Airport</a> (approx. 120 km away) for domestic flights.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The city today is at the junction of the two most important highways in all of the Saudi Arabian highway system, Highway 40, which connects the city to Jeddah in the west and the capital, <a href="/wiki/Riyadh" title="Riyadh">Riyadh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dammam" title="Dammam">Dammam</a> in the east and Highway 15, which connects it to <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tabuk,_Saudi_Arabia" title="Tabuk, Saudi Arabia">Tabuk</a> and onward to <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> in the north and <a href="/wiki/Abha" title="Abha">Abha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jizan" title="Jizan">Jizan</a> in the south. The Ottomans had planned to extend their railway network to the holy city, but were forced to abandon this plan due to their entry into the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>. This plan was later carried out by the Saudi government, which connected the two holy cities of Medina and Mecca with the modern <a href="/wiki/Haramain_high-speed_railway" title="Haramain high-speed railway">Haramain high-speed railway</a> system which runs at 300 km/h (190 mph) and connects the two cities via Jeddah, King Abdulaziz International Airport and <a href="/wiki/King_Abdullah_Economic_City" title="King Abdullah Economic City">King Abdullah Economic City</a> near Rabigh within two hours.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Haram_(site)" title="Haram (site)">haram area</a> of Mecca, in which the entry of non-Muslims is forbidden, is much larger than that of Medina.
</p>
<p><b>1979 Grand Mosque seizure</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></p><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1979_Grand_Mosque_seizure" title="1979 Grand Mosque seizure">1979 Grand Mosque seizure</a></div>
<p>On 20 November 1979, two hundred armed dissidents led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juhayman_al-Otaibi" title="Juhayman al-Otaibi">Juhayman al-Otaibi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Mosque_Seizure" title="Grand Mosque Seizure">seized the Grand Mosque</a>, claiming the Saudi royal family no longer represented pure Islam and that the <a href="/wiki/Masjid_al-Haram" title="Masjid al-Haram">Masjid al-Haram</a> and the Ka'bah, must be held by those of true faith. The rebels seized tens of thousands of pilgrims as hostages and barricaded themselves in the <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a>. The siege lasted two weeks, and resulted in several hundred deaths and significant damage to the shrine, especially the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Safa_and_Al-Marwah" title="Al-Safa and Al-Marwah">Safa-Marwah</a> gallery. A multinational force was finally able to retake the mosque from the dissidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Since then, the Grand Mosque has been expanded several times, with many other expansions being undertaken in the present day.
</p>
<p><b>Destruction of Islamic heritage sites</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></p><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_early_Islamic_heritage_sites_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Destruction of early Islamic heritage sites in Saudi Arabia">Destruction of early Islamic heritage sites in Saudi Arabia</a></div>
<p>Under Saudi rule, it has been estimated that since 1985, about 95% of Mecca's historic buildings, most over a thousand years old, have been demolished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-89">[88]</a></sup> It has been reported that there are now fewer than 20 structures remaining in Mecca that date back to the time of Muhammad. Some important buildings that have been destroyed include the house of <a href="/wiki/Khadija_bint_Khuwaylid" title="Khadija bint Khuwaylid">Khadijah</a>, the wife of Muhammad, the house of <a href="/wiki/Abu_Bakr" title="Abu Bakr">Abu Bakr</a>, Muhammad's birthplace and the Ottoman-era <a href="/wiki/Ajyad_Fortress" title="Ajyad Fortress">Ajyad Fortress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> The reason for much of the destruction of historic buildings has been for the construction of hotels, apartments, parking lots, and other infrastructure facilities for <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> pilgrims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-89">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<p><b>Incidents during pilgrimage</b><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></p><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Incidents_during_the_Hajj" title="Incidents during the Hajj">Incidents during the Hajj</a></div>
<p>Mecca has been the site of several incidents and failures of crowd control because of the large numbers of people who come to make the Hajj.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> For example, on 2 July 1990, a pilgrimage to Mecca ended in tragedy when the ventilation system failed in a crowded pedestrian tunnel and 1,426 people were either suffocated or trampled to death in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1990_Hajj_stampede" title="1990 Hajj stampede">stampede</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> On 24 September 2015, 700 pilgrims <a href="/wiki/2015_Mina_stampede" title="2015 Mina stampede">were killed</a> in a stampede at <a href="/wiki/Mina,_Saudi_Arabia" title="Mina, Saudi Arabia">Mina</a> during the stoning-the-Devil ritual at Jamarat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Significance_in_Islam">Significance in Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Significance in Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Mecque_pelerinage.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="792" data-file-width="1104" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/La_Mecque_pelerinage.png/220px-La_Mecque_pelerinage.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/La_Mecque_pelerinage.png/330px-La_Mecque_pelerinage.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/La_Mecque_pelerinage.png/440px-La_Mecque_pelerinage.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_Mecque_pelerinage.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> involves pilgrims visiting Al-Haram Mosque, but mainly camping and spending time in the plains of <a href="/wiki/Mina,_Saudi_Arabia" title="Mina, Saudi Arabia">Mina</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arafah" title="Arafah">Arafah</a></div></div></div>
<p>Mecca holds an important place in Islam and is the holiest city in all branches of the religion. The city derives its importance from the role it plays in the <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a> and '<a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Masjid_al-Haram">Masjid al-Haram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Masjid al-Haram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Masjid al-Haram</i> is the site of two of the most important rites of both the Hajj and of the Umrah, the circumambulation around the Ka'bah (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tawaf" title="Tawaf">tawaf</a></i>) and the walking between the two mounts of Safa and Marwa (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sa%27ee" title="Sa'ee">sa'ee</a></i>). The masjid is also the site of the <a href="/wiki/Zamzam_Well" title="Zamzam Well">Zamzam Well</a>. According to Islamic tradition, a prayer in the masjid is equal to 100,000 prayers in any other masjid around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kaaba">Kaaba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Kaaba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">Kaaba</a></div>
<p>There is a difference of opinion between Islamic scholars upon who first built the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ka%27bah" title="Ka'bah">Ka'bah</a>, some believe it was built by the <a href="/wiki/Angels_in_Islam" title="Angels in Islam">angels</a> while others believe it was built by <a href="/wiki/Adam_and_Eve" title="Adam and Eve">Adam</a>. Regardless, it was built several times before reaching its current state. The Ka'bah is also the common direction of prayer (<i><a href="/wiki/Qibla" title="Qibla">qibla</a></i>) for all Muslims. The surface surrounding the Ka'bah on which Muslims circumambulate it is known as the Mataf.
</p>
<h4><span id="Hijr_al-Aswad_.28The_Black_Stone.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hijr_al-Aswad_(The_Black_Stone)">Hijr al-Aswad (The Black Stone)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hijr al-Aswad (The Black Stone)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Black_Stone" title="Black Stone">Black Stone</a></div>
<p>The Black Stone is a stone, considered by scientists to be a <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">meteorite</a> or of similar origin and believed by Muslims to be of divine origin. It is set in the eastern corner of the Ka’bah and it is <a href="/wiki/Sunnah" title="Sunnah">Sunnah</a> to touch and kiss the stone. The area around the stone is generally always crowded and guarded by policemen to ensure the pilgrims' safety.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maqam_Ibrahim">Maqam Ibrahim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Maqam Ibrahim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This is the stone that Ibraham(Abraham) stood on to build the higher parts of the Ka'bah. It contains two footprints that are comparatively larger than average modern-day human feet. The stone is raised and housed in a golden hexagonal chamber beside the Ka'bah on the Mataf plate.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Safa_and_Marwa">Safa and Marwa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Safa and Marwa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Safa_and_Marwa" title="Safa and Marwa">Safa and Marwa</a></div><p>
Muslims believe that in the divine revelation to Muhammad, the Quran, Allah describes the mountains of Safa and Marwah as symbols of his divinity. Walking between the two mountains seven times, 4 times from Safa to Marwah and 3 times from Marwah interchangeably, is considered a mandatory pillar (<i><a href="/wiki/Fard" title="Fard">rukn</a></i>) of '<a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a>.</p><div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1132px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG" title="Panorama of the al-Masjid al-Haram, also known as the Grand Mosque of Mecca, during the Hajj pilgrimage"><img alt="" data-file-height="972" data-file-width="5464" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG/1124px-Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG/1686px-Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG/2248px-Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG 2x" width="1124"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Masjid_al-Haram_panorama.JPG" title="File:Masjid al-Haram panorama.JPG"> </a></div>Panorama of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Masjid_al-Haram" title="Al-Masjid al-Haram">al-Masjid al-Haram</a>, also known as the Grand Mosque of Mecca, during the Hajj pilgrimage</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Hajj_and_.27Umrah"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hajj_and_'Umrah">Hajj and 'Umrah</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hajj and 'Umrah">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
The Hajj pilgrimage also called the greater pilgrimage, attracts millions of Muslims from all over the world and almost triples Mecca's population for one week in the twelfth and final Islamic month of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhu_al-Hijjah" title="Dhu al-Hijjah">Dhu al-Hijjah</a></i>. In 2019, the Hajj attracted 2,489,406 pilgrims to the holy city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> The 'Umrah, or the lesser pilgrimage, can be done at anytime during the year.  Every adult, healthy Muslim who has the financial and physical capacity to travel to Mecca must perform the Hajj at least once in a lifetime. Umrah, the lesser pilgrimage, is not obligatory, but is recommended in the Quran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> In addition to the <i>Masjid al-Haram</i>, pilgrims also must visit the nearby towns of <a href="/wiki/Mina,_Saudi_Arabia" title="Mina, Saudi Arabia">Mina/Muna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muzdalifah" title="Muzdalifah">Muzdalifah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Arafat" title="Mount Arafat">Mount Arafat</a> for various rituals that are part of the Hajj.</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jabal_Nur.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Jabal_Nur.JPG/220px-Jabal_Nur.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Jabal_Nur.JPG/330px-Jabal_Nur.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Jabal_Nur.JPG/440px-Jabal_Nur.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jabal_Nur.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jabal_al-Nour" title="Jabal al-Nour">Jabal al-Nour</a>, the mountain atop which is the Hira cave, where it is believed Muhammad received his first revelation.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jabal_an-Nur">Jabal an-Nur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Jabal an-Nur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This is a mountain believed by Muslims to have been the place where Muhammad spent his time away from the bustling city of Mecca in seclusion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-101">[100]</a></sup> The mountain is located on the eastern entrance of the city and is the highest point in the city at 642 meters (2,106 feet).
</p>
<h4><span id="Hira.27a_Cave"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hira'a_Cave">Hira'a Cave</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hira'a Cave">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Situated atop Jabal an-Nur, this is the place where Muslims believe Muhammad received the first revelation from Allah through the archangel <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Gabriel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Angels_in_Islam" title="Angels in Islam">Jibril</a> in Islamic tradition) at the age of 40.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-100">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-101">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg/220px-Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg/330px-Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg/440px-Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Quran Gate</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS-44_Mecca,_Saudi_Arabia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3280" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/ISS-44_Mecca%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/220px-ISS-44_Mecca%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/ISS-44_Mecca%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/330px-ISS-44_Mecca%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/ISS-44_Mecca%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/440px-ISS-44_Mecca%2C_Saudi_Arabia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS-44_Mecca,_Saudi_Arabia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mecca as seen from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a></div></div></div><p>Mecca is located in the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz region</a>, a 200 km (124 mi) wide strip of mountains separating the <a href="/wiki/An_Nafud" title="An Nafud">Nafud desert</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. The city is situated in a valley with the same name around 70 km (44 mi) west of the port city of <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>. Mecca is one of the lowest cities in elevation in the Hejaz region, located at an elevation of 277 m (909 ft) above sea level at 21º23' north latitude and 39º51' east longitude. Mecca is divided into 34 districts.
</p><p>The city centers on the al-Haram area, which contains the Masjid al-Haram. The area around the mosque is the old city and contains the most famous district of Mecca, Ajyad. The main street that runs to <i>al-Haram</i> is the Ibrahim al-Khalil Street, named after <a href="/wiki/Abraham_in_Islam" title="Abraham in Islam">Ibrahim</a>. Traditional, historical homes built of local rock, two to three stories long are still present within the city's central area, within view of modern hotels and shopping complexes. The total area of modern Mecca is over 1,200 km<sup>2</sup> (460 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elevation">Elevation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Elevation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mecca is at an elevation of 277 m (909 ft) above sea level, and approximately 70 km (44 mi) inland from the Red Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-world-13_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-world-13-67">[66]</a></sup> It is one of the lowest in the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> region.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city center lies in a corridor between mountains, which is often called the "Hollow of Mecca". The area contains the valley of al-Taneem, the valley of Bakkah and the valley of Abqar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIE_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-EIE-64">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup> This mountainous location has defined the contemporary expansion of the city.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources_of_water">Sources of water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sources of water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In pre-modern Mecca, the city used a few chief sources of water. The first were local wells, such as the Zamzam Well, that produced generally brackish water. The second source was the spring of 'Ayn Zubaydah (Spring of Zubaydah). The sources of this spring are the mountains of Jabal Sa'd and Jabal Kabkāb, which are a few kilometers east of 'Arafah/'Arafat or about 20 km (12 mi) southeast of Mecca. Water was transported from it using underground channels. A very sporadic third source was rainfall which was stored by the people in small reservoirs or <a href="/wiki/Cistern" title="Cistern">cisterns</a>. The rainfall, scant as it is, also presents the threat of flooding and has been a danger since earliest times. According to al-Kurdī, there had been 89 floods by 1965. In the last century, the most severe flood was that of 1942. Since then, dams have been built to ameliorate this problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
Mecca features a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: <i>BWh</i>), in three different <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">plant hardiness zones</a>: 10, 11 and 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> Like most Saudi Arabian cities, Mecca retains warm to hot temperatures even in winter, which can range from 19 °C (66 °F) at night to 30 °C (86 °F) in the afternoon, but also, very rarely, fall to zero and subzero temperatures. Summer temperatures are extremely hot and consistently break the 40 °C (104 °F) mark in the afternoon, dropping to 30 °C (86 °F) in the evening, but humidity remains relatively low, at 30–40%. Rain usually falls in Mecca in small amounts scattered between November and January, with heavy thunderstorms also common during the winter.</p><div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Meccan economy has been heavily dependent on the annual pilgrimage. Income generated from the Hajj, in fact, not only powers the Meccan economy but has historically had far-reaching effects on the economy of the entire <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a>. The income was generated in a number of ways. One method was taxing the pilgrims. Taxes were especially increased during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, and many of these taxes existed to as late as 1972. Another way the Hajj generates income is through services to pilgrims. For example, the Saudi <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudia" title="Saudia">Saudia</a>, generates 12% of its income from the pilgrimage. Fares paid by pilgrims to reach Mecca by land also generate income; as do the hotels and lodging companies that house them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-2"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup> The city takes in more than $100 million, while the Saudi government spends about $50 million on services for the Hajj. There are some industries and factories in the city, but Mecca no longer plays a major role in Saudi Arabia's economy, which is mainly based on oil exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> The few industries operating in Mecca include textiles, furniture, and utensils. The majority of the economy is service-oriented.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg/220px-Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg/330px-Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg/440px-Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Makkah_Azizia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i>al-'Aziziyah</i> district of Mecca</div></div></div>
<p>Nevertheless, many industries have been set up in Mecca. Various types of enterprises that have existed since 1970 in the city include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_mining" title="Iron mining">corrugated iron manufacturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper_extraction" title="Copper extraction">copper extraction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carpentry" title="Carpentry">carpentry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upholstery" title="Upholstery">upholstery</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakeries" title="Bakeries">bakeries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farm" title="Farm">farming</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banking" title="Banking">banking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-3"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup> The city has grown substantially in the 20th and 21st centuries, as the convenience and affordability of <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jet</a> travel has increased the number of pilgrims participating in the <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a>. Thousands of Saudis are employed year-round to oversee the Hajj and staff the hotels and shops that cater to pilgrims; these workers in turn have increased the demand for housing and services. The city is now ringed by freeways, and contains shopping malls and skyscrapers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_resources">Human resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Human resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Formal education started to be developed in the late Ottoman period continuing slowly into Hashemite times. The first major attempt to improve the situation was made by a Jeddah merchant, Muhammad ʿAlī Zaynal Riḍā, who founded the Madrasat al-Falāḥ in Mecca in 1911–12 that cost £400,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-4"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup> The school system in Mecca has many public and private schools for both males and females. As of 2005, there were 532 <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">public</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_school" title="Private school">private schools</a> for males and another 681 public and private schools for female students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> The medium of instruction in both public and private schools is Arabic with emphasis on English as a <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">second language</a>, but some private schools founded by foreign entities such as <a href="/wiki/International_school" title="International school">International schools</a> use the English language as the medium of instruction. Some of these are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coeducation" title="Coeducation">coeducational</a> while other schools are not. For higher education, the city has only one university, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umm_Al-Qura_University" title="Umm Al-Qura University">Umm Al-Qura University</a>, which was established in 1949 as a college and became a public university in 1981.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Healthcare is provided by the Saudi government free of charge to all pilgrims. There are ten main hospitals in Mecca:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Ajyad Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى أَجْيَاد</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>King Faisal Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى ٱلْمَلِك فَيْصَل بِحَي ٱلشّشه</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>King Abdulaziz Hospital (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى ٱلْمَلِك عَبْد ٱلْعَزِيْز بِحَي ٱلـزَّاهِر</span>‎</span>)</li>
<li>Al Noor Specialist Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى ٱلنُّوْر ٱلتَّخَصُّصِي</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>Hira'a Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى حِرَاء</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>Maternity and Children's Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى ٱلْوِلَادَة وَٱلْأَطْفَال</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>King Abdullah Medical City (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مَدِيْنَة ٱلْمَلِك عَبْد ٱلله ٱلطِّبِيَّة</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>Khulais General Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى خُلَيْص ٱلْعَام</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>Al Kamel General Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى ٱلْكَامِل ٱلْعَام</span>‎</span></span>)</li>
<li>Ibn Sina Hospital (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097707674" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">مُسْتَشْفَى ابْن سِيْنَا بِحَدَاء / بَحْرَه</span>‎</span></span>)</li></ul>
<p>There are also many walk-in clinics available for both residents and pilgrims. Several temporary clinics are set up during the Hajj to tend to wounded pilgrims.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic">Effect of the COVID-19 pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Effect of the COVID-19 pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_Hajj" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on Hajj">Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on Hajj</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mecca,_July_2021_25.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Mecca%2C_July_2021_25.jpg/220px-Mecca%2C_July_2021_25.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Mecca%2C_July_2021_25.jpg/330px-Mecca%2C_July_2021_25.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Mecca%2C_July_2021_25.jpg/440px-Mecca%2C_July_2021_25.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mecca,_July_2021_25.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kaaba in July 2021, during COVID-19 restrictions.</div></div></div>
<p>In February 2020, Saudi Arabia temporarily banned foreigners from entering Mecca and <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a> to mitigate the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Saudi Arabia">in the Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mecca.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mecca.JPG/220px-Mecca.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mecca.JPG/330px-Mecca.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mecca.JPG/440px-Mecca.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mecca.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Al-Haram Mosque and the <a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">Kaaba</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg/220px-Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg/330px-Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg/440px-Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kaaba_during_expansion_in_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kaaba during expansion in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Mecca's culture has been affected by the large number of pilgrims that arrive annually, and thus boasts a rich <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">cultural heritage</a>. As a result of the vast numbers of pilgrims coming to the city each year, Mecca has become by far the most diverse city in the Muslim world.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Baik" title="Al Baik">Al Baik</a>, a local fast-food chain, is very popular among pilgrims and locals alike. Until 2018, it was available only in Mecca, <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, and traveling to Jeddah just to get a taste of the fried chicken was common.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In pre-modern Mecca, the most common sports were impromptu wrestling and foot races.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-5"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is now the most popular sport in Mecca and the kingdom, and the city hosts some of the oldest sport clubs in Saudi Arabia such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Wahda_(Mecca)" title="Al-Wahda (Mecca)">Al Wahda FC</a> (established in 1945). <a href="/wiki/King_Abdul_Aziz_Stadium" title="King Abdul Aziz Stadium">King Abdulaziz Stadium</a> is the largest stadium in Mecca with a capacity of 38,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mecca is very densely populated. Most long-term residents live in the Old City, the area around the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Mecca" title="Great Mosque of Mecca">Great Mosque</a> and many work to support pilgrims, known locally as the <i>Hajj</i> industry. 'Iyad Madani, the Saudi Arabian Minister for Hajj, was quoted saying, "We never stop preparing for the Hajj."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>Year-round, pilgrims stream into the city to perform the rites of '<a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a>, and during the last weeks of eleventh Islamic month, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhu_al-Qi%27dah" title="Dhu al-Qi'dah">Dhu al-Qi'dah</a>, on average 2–4 million Muslims arrive in the city to take part in the rites known as Hajj.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebmm_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-ebmm-114">[113]</a></sup> Pilgrims are from varying <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnicities</a> and backgrounds, mainly <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, Europe and Africa. Many of these pilgrims have remained and become residents of the city. The Burmese are an older, more established community who number roughly 250,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Adding to this, the discovery of oil in the past 50 years has brought hundreds of thousands of working immigrants.
</p><p>Non-Muslims are not permitted to enter Mecca under <a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Basic Law of Saudi Arabia">Saudi law</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peters_206_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-peters_206-13">[12]</a></sup> and using fraudulent documents to do so may result in arrest and prosecution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> The prohibition extends to <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadis</a>, as they are considered non-Muslims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> Nevertheless, many non-Muslims and Ahmadis have visited the city as these restrictions are loosely enforced. The first such recorded example of a non-Muslim entering the city is that of <a href="/wiki/Ludovico_di_Varthema" title="Ludovico di Varthema">Ludovico di Varthema</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a> in 1503.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Guru_Nanak" title="Guru Nanak">Guru Nanak</a>, the founder of Sikhism, is said to have visited Mecca<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> in December 1518.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> One of the most famous was <a href="/wiki/Richard_Francis_Burton" title="Richard Francis Burton">Richard Francis Burton</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> who traveled as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qadiriyyah" title="Qadiriyyah">Qadiriyya</a> <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> from <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> in 1853.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mecca_Province" title="Mecca Province">Mecca Province</a> is the only province where <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a> outnumber <a href="/wiki/Saudis" title="Saudis">Saudis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architectural_landmarks">Architectural landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Architectural landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Adorning the southern facade of the Masjid al-Haram, the <a href="/wiki/Abraj_Al_Bait" title="Abraj Al Bait">Abraj al-Bait Complex</a>, which towers over the Great Mosque, is a seven-building complex with the central clock tower having a length of 601 m (1,972 feet), making it the world's fourth-tallest building. All seven buildings in the complex also form the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_buildings_in_the_world" title="List of largest buildings in the world">third-largest building by floor area</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mecca_Gate" title="Mecca Gate">Mecca Gate</a>, known popularly as the Quran Gate, on the western entrance of the city, or from Jeddah. Located on Highway 40, it marks the boundary of the <a href="/wiki/Haram_(site)" title="Haram (site)">Haram area</a> where non-Muslims are prohibited from entering. The gate was designed in 1979 by an Egyptian architect, Samir Elabd, for the architectural firm IDEA Center. The structure is that of a book, representing the Quran, sitting on a <a href="/wiki/Rehal_(book_rest)" title="Rehal (book rest)"><i>rehal</i></a>, or bookrest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Makkah_Gate_Design_-_elabdarchitecture.com_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Makkah_Gate_Design_-_elabdarchitecture.com-123">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press_and_newspapers">Press and newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Press and newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first press was brought to Mecca in 1885 by <a href="/wiki/Osman_Nuri_Pasha" title="Osman Nuri Pasha">Osman Nuri Pasha</a>, an Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Wali_(administrative_title)" title="Wali (administrative title)">Wāli</a>. During the Hashemite period, it was used to print the city's official gazette, <i><a href="/wiki/Al_Qibla" title="Al Qibla">Al Qibla</a></i>. The Saudi regime expanded this press into a larger operation, introducing the new Saudi official gazette of Mecca, <i>Umm al-Qurā</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-6"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup> Mecca also has its own paper owned by the city, <i><a href="/wiki/Al_Nadwa" title="Al Nadwa">Al Nadwa</a></i>. However, other Saudi newspapers are also provided in Mecca such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Gazette" title="Saudi Gazette">Saudi Gazette</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Madinah" title="Al Madinah">Al Madinah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Okaz" title="Okaz">Okaz</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Al-Bilad_(Saudi_newspaper)" title="Al-Bilad (Saudi newspaper)">Al Bilad</a>,</i> in addition to other international newspapers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TV">TV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: TV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Telecommunications in the city were emphasized early under the Saudi reign. King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_Saud_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Ibn Saud of Saudi Arabia">Abdulaziz</a> pressed them forward as he saw them as a means of convenience and better governance. While under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_Sharif_of_Mecca" title="Hussein bin Ali, Sharif of Mecca">Hussein bin Ali</a>, there were about 20 public telephones in the entire city; in 1936, the number jumped to 450, totaling about half the telephones in the country. During that time, telephone lines were extended to Jeddah and Ta’if, but not to the capital, <a href="/wiki/Riyadh" title="Riyadh">Riyadh</a>. By 1985, Mecca, like other Saudi cities, possessed modern telephone, telex, radio and television communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-7"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup> Many television stations serving the city area include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saudi_T.V._Channel_1" title="Saudi T.V. Channel 1">Saudi TV1</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saudi_T.V._Channel_II" title="Saudi T.V. Channel II">Saudi TV2</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saudi_TV_Sports" title="Saudi TV Sports">Saudi TV Sports</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Ekhbariya" title="Al-Ekhbariya">Al-Ekhbariya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_Radio_and_Television_Network" title="Arab Radio and Television Network">Arab Radio and Television Network</a> and various cable, satellite and other specialty television providers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Limited radio communication was established within the Kingdom under the Hashemites. In 1929, wireless stations were set up in various towns in the region, creating a network that would become fully functional by 1932. Soon after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the existing network was greatly expanded and improved. Since then, radio communication has been used extensively in directing the pilgrimage and addressing the pilgrims. This practice started in 1950, with the initiation of broadcasts on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Day_of_Arafa" title="Day of Arafa">Day of 'Arafah</a> (9 Dhu al-Hijjah), and increased until 1957, at which time Radio Makkah became the most powerful station in the Middle East at 50 kW. Later, power was increased 9-fold to 450 kW. Music was not immediately broadcast, but gradually folk music was introduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIModern_103-8"><a href="#cite_note-EIModern-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KAAirport-NT.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/KAAirport-NT.JPG/220px-KAAirport-NT.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/KAAirport-NT.JPG/330px-KAAirport-NT.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/KAAirport-NT.JPG/440px-KAAirport-NT.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KAAirport-NT.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hajj terminal</div></div></div>
<p>The only airport near the city is the Mecca East airport, which is not active. Mecca is primarily served by <a href="/wiki/King_Abdulaziz_International_Airport" title="King Abdulaziz International Airport">King Abdulaziz International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a> for international and regional connections and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%27if_Regional_Airport" title="Ta'if Regional Airport">Ta'if Regional Airport</a> for regional connections. To cater the large number of Hajj pilgrims, Jeddah Airport has Hajj Terminal, specifically for use in the <i>Hajj</i> season, which can accommodate 47 planes simultaneously and can receive 3,800 pilgrims per hour during the Hajj season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening1_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening1-124">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="421" data-file-width="699" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg/220px-Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg/330px-Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg/440px-Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entry-Gate-of-Mecca-on-Jaddah-Makkah-Highway.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entry Gate of Mecca on Highway 40</div></div></div>
<p>Mecca, similar to Medina, lies at the junction of two of the most important highways in Saudi Arabia, <a href="/wiki/Highway_40_(Saudi_Arabia)" title="Highway 40 (Saudi Arabia)">Highway 40</a>, connecting it to the important port city of <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a> in the west and the capital of <a href="/wiki/Riyadh" title="Riyadh">Riyadh</a> and the other major port city, <a href="/wiki/Dammam" title="Dammam">Dammam</a>, in the east. The other, Highway 15, connects Mecca to the other holy Islamic city of Medina approximately 400 km (250 mi) in the north and onward to <a href="/wiki/Tabuk,_Saudi_Arabia" title="Tabuk, Saudi Arabia">Tabuk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>. While in the south, it connects Mecca to <a href="/wiki/Abha" title="Abha">Abha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jizan" title="Jizan">Jizan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> Mecca is served by four ring roads, and these are very crowded compared to the three ring roads of Medina.
</p><p>Mecca also has many tunnels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rapid_transit">Rapid transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Rapid transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Al Masha'er Al Muqaddassah Metro</b>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Mashaaer_Al_Mugaddassah_Metro" title="Al Mashaaer Al Mugaddassah Metro">Al Masha'er Al Muqaddassah Metro</a> is a metro line in Mecca opened on 13 November 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening2_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening2-128">[127]</a></sup> The 18.1-kilometer (11.2-mile) elevated metro transports pilgrims to the holy sites of '<a href="/wiki/Mount_Arafat" title="Mount Arafat">Arafat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muzdalifah" title="Muzdalifah">Muzdalifah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mina,_Saudi_Arabia" title="Mina, Saudi Arabia">Mina</a> in the city to reduce congestion on the road and is only operational during the <i><a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a></i> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rgi20090624_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20090624-129">[128]</a></sup> It consists of nine stations, three in each of the aforementioned towns.
</p>
<p><b>Mecca Metro</b></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1020" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png/220px-Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png/330px-Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png/440px-Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mecca_Metro_Route_Map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mecca Metro Route Map</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mecca_Metro" title="Mecca Metro">Mecca Metro</a>, officially known as <b>Makkah Mass Rail Transit</b>, is a planned four-line <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system for the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-approved_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-approved-130">[129]</a></sup> This will be in addition to<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-approved_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-approved-130">[129]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Mashaaer_Al_Mugaddassah_Metro" title="Al Mashaaer Al Mugaddassah Metro">Al Masha'er Al Muqaddassah Metro</a> which carries pilgrims.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Intercity">Intercity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Intercity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2018, a high speed intercity rail line, part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haramain_High_Speed_Rail_Project" title="Haramain High Speed Rail Project">Haramain High Speed Rail Project</a>, named the <a href="/wiki/Haramain_high-speed_railway" title="Haramain high-speed railway">Haramain high-speed railway</a> line entered operation, connecting the holy cities of Mecca and <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a> together via <a href="/wiki/Jeddah" title="Jeddah">Jeddah</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_Abdulaziz_International_Airport" title="King Abdulaziz International Airport">King Abdulaziz International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/King_Abdullah_Economic_City" title="King Abdullah Economic City">King Abdullah Economic City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rabigh" title="Rabigh">Rabigh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rgi20090423_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20090423-131">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arabnews_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arabnews-132">[131]</a></sup> The railway consists of 35 <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">electric trains</a> and is capable of transporting 60 million passengers annually. Each train can achieve speeds of up to 300 kmh (190 mph), traveling a total distance of 450 km (280 mi), reducing the travel time between the two cities to less than two hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arwmmcc_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-arwmmcc-133">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arabnews_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Arabnews-132">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mecca&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-Britannica-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Britannica_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.britannica.com/topic/Wahhabi" rel="nofollow">"Wahhābī (Islamic movement)"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>: <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica,_Inc." title="Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.">Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.</a> 9 June 2020. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200626201633/https://www.britannica.com/topic/Wahhabi" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 26 June 2020<span class="reference-accessdate">.
